\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01834}01834 \(\backslash\)f[ }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01835}01835 p(x\_k) = \(\backslash\)sum\_\{j=1\}\string^\{N\_P\} P\_j \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)psi\string^\{(P)\}\_j(x\_k). \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)  (9)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01836}01836 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01837}01837 The number of nodes involved in the representation of}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01838}01838 the velocity, \(\backslash\)f\$N\(\backslash\)f\$, can (and usually does) differ from the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01839}01839 number of nodes involved in the representation of the pressure,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01840}01840 \(\backslash\)f\$N\_P\(\backslash\)f\$.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01841}01841 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01842}01842 Stability constraints (the infamous LBB *REFERENCE*condition) impose}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01843}01843 certain restrictions on the choice of basis functions. }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01844}01844 One well-\/known stable discretisation employs piecewise quadratic interpolations}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01845}01845 for the velocities and a piecewise linear interpolation for the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01846}01846 pressure. The resulting elements are known as "{}Taylor-\/Hood"{} elements. }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01847}01847 When implemented as an isoparametric, 2D quadrilateral element, the }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01848}01848 element geometry and the velocity components are represented }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01849}01849 by the bi-\/quadratic local shape functions \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)psi\_j(x\_k)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01850}01850 \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) (j=1,...,9)\(\backslash\)f\$ which interpolate between the nodal values}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01851}01851 and coordinates of the element's \(\backslash\)f\$ n=9 \(\backslash\)f\$ local nodes. }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01852}01852 The pressure is represented in terms of the bilinear local shape functions, }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01853}01853 \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)psi\string^\{(P)\}\_j(x\_k) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) (j=1,...,4)\(\backslash\)f\$, which interpolate between }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01854}01854 pressure values at the element's  \(\backslash\)f\$ n\_p=4 \(\backslash\)f\$ corner nodes, as }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01855}01855 shown in this sketch:}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01856}01856 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01857}01857 \(\backslash\)image html taylor\_hood.gif "{}Velocity (blue) and pressure (red) nodes in a quadrilateral Taylor-\/Hood "{} }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01858}01858 \(\backslash\)image latex taylor\_hood.eps "{}Velocity (blue) and pressure (red) nodes in a quadrilateral Taylor-\/Hood "{} width=0.35\(\backslash\)textwidth}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01859}01859 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01860}01860 In this case, the number of nodal values is not the same for each}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01861}01861 node: the corner nodes store two velocity components and one pressure;}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01862}01862 all other nodes only store the two velocity components.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01863}01863 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01864}01864  The weak form of the Navier-\/Stokes equations is obtained by}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01865}01865 using the pressure shape functions \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)psi\string^\{(P)\}\_j(s\_k)\(\backslash\)f\$ as the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01866}01866 test functions for the continuity equation and the velocity shape}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01867}01867 functions to test the momentum equations. Upon performing the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01868}01868 usual integration by parts and using the divergence}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01869}01869 theorem (Exercise!), the (global) residuals}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01870}01870 are then given by}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01871}01871 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01872}01872 f\_\{il\} = \(\backslash\)int\_D  \(\backslash\)left[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01873}01873 \(\backslash\)left( Re \(\backslash\)sum\_\{k=1\}\string^2  u\_k  \(\backslash\)frac\{\(\backslash\)partial u\_i\}\{\(\backslash\)partial x\_k\} \(\backslash\)right)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01874}01874 \(\backslash\)psi\_l -\/ p \(\backslash\)frac\{\(\backslash\)partial \(\backslash\)psi\_l\}\{\(\backslash\)partial x\_i\} +  }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01875}01875 \(\backslash\)sum\_\{k=1\}\string^2 \(\backslash\)frac\{\(\backslash\)partial u\_i\}\{\(\backslash\)partial x\_k\} }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01876}01876              \(\backslash\)frac\{\(\backslash\)partial \(\backslash\)psi\_l\}\{\(\backslash\)partial x\_k\} \(\backslash\)right] dV = 0,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01877}01877 \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) (10)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01878}01878 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01879}01879 where we have ignored any boundary terms (hence, implying }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01880}01880 the velocity is prescribed along the entire domain boundary), }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01881}01881 and }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01882}01882 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01883}01883 f\_\{l\}\string^\{(P)\} = \(\backslash\)int\_D  \(\backslash\)left( \(\backslash\)sum\_\{k=1\}\string^2}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01884}01884  \(\backslash\)frac\{\(\backslash\)partial u\_k\}\{\(\backslash\)partial x\_k\} \(\backslash\)right) \(\backslash\)psi\string^\{(P)\}\_l  dV = 0.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01885}01885 \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) (11)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01886}01886 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01887}01887 The system of nonlinear algebraic equations (10)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01888}01888 provides one equation, \(\backslash\)f\$ f\_\{il\} \(\backslash\)f\$, for each velocity}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01889}01889 component \(\backslash\)f\$ (i=1,2) \(\backslash\)f\$ at those nodes \(\backslash\)f\$(l=1,...,N)\(\backslash\)f\$ where}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01890}01890 the velocity is not prescribed by a Dirichlet boundary condition.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01891}01891 The weak continuity equations (11) provides }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01892}01892 the remaining  equations \(\backslash\)f\$ f\_\{l\}\string^\{(P)\} =0 \(\backslash\)f\$ for the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01893}01893 pressure values  \(\backslash\)f\$ P\_j \(\backslash\) (j=1,...,N\_p)\(\backslash\)f\$ that are not prescribed.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01894}01894 [Usually there are no boundary conditions for the pressure -\/-\/ the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01895}01895 pressure can only be set indirectly through applied-\/traction boundary }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01896}01896 conditions in which the normal component of the applied traction}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01897}01897 contains a contribution from the pressure and the viscous normal stresses; only}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01898}01898 if the velocity is prescribed along the entire boundary is it legal,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01899}01899 and, in fact, necessary,  to pin a single pressure value.]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01900}01900 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01901}01901 <B>Implementation</B> \(\backslash\)n\(\backslash\)n}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01902}01902 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01903}01903 The implementation of an element with continuous }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01904}01904 mixed interpolation is straightforward:}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01905}01905 -\/ The function \(\backslash\)c FiniteElement:required\_nvalue(...) needs to specify}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01906}01906   the required number of values for each node.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01907}01907 -\/ The element can "{}recycle"{} the geometric shape functions to implement}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01908}01908   the isoparametric representation of the velocity components. }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01909}01909 -\/ The element needs to define another set of basis functions }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01910}01910   which is used to represent the pressure.  }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01911}01911 -\/ The local equation numbering scheme needs to be augmented to }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01912}01912   include the pressure degrees of freedom. }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01913}01913 .}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01914}01914 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01915}01915 <HR>}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01916}01916 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01917}01917 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01918}01918 \(\backslash\)subsection discontinuous\_interpolation Discontinuous interpolation -\/-\/ "{}Internal Data"{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01919}01919 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01920}01920 The choice of basis functions in Taylor-\/Hood-\/type Navier-\/Stokes elements}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01921}01921 appears to be perfectly natural. The bi-\/quadratic interpolation of the velocity}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01922}01922 components between the element's nodal values enforces the inter-\/element }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01923}01923 continuity of the velocity, which ensures that the integrals in}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01924}01924 (10) "{}make sense"{}. The LBB constraint requires the }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01925}01925 use of a lower-\/order representation for the pressure; the "{}obvious"{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01926}01926 choice is bilinear }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01927}01927 interpolation between the pressure values at the four corner nodes,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01928}01928 which also ensures inter-\/element continuity of the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01929}01929 pressure. An}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01930}01930 inspection of the weak form of the Navier-\/Stokes equations, }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01931}01931 (10) and (11),}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01932}01932 shows that this is not strictly required because the integration by parts has}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01933}01933 removed the derivatives on the pressure. Hence the weak form "{}makes}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01934}01934 sense"{} even if the pressure is globally discontinuous. This suggests the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01935}01935 use of different types of basis functions for the representation of}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01936}01936 the pressure. An example is given by the Crouzeix-\/Raviart Navier-\/Stokes }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01937}01937 elements in which the pressure within each element is represented }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01938}01938 by the three basis functions}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01939}01939 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01940}01940 \(\backslash\)psi\_1\string^\{(P)\}(s\_1,s\_2) = 1,\(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)  }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01941}01941 \(\backslash\)psi\_2\string^\{(P)\}(s\_1,s\_2) = s\_1,\(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)  }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01942}01942 \(\backslash\)psi\_3\string^\{(P)\}(s\_1,s\_2) = s\_2,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01943}01943 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01944}01944 so that the pressure in element \(\backslash\)f\$ e \(\backslash\)f\$ is given by the complete}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01945}01945 linear polynomial,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01946}01946 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01947}01947 p(s\_1,s\_2) = \(\backslash\)sum\_\{j\_p=1\}\string^3 P\_\{j\_p e\}  \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)psi\_j\string^\{(P)\}(s\_1,s\_2).}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01948}01948 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01949}01949 In this representation, the discrete pressure values,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01950}01950 \(\backslash\)f\$P\_\{j\_p e\}\(\backslash\)f\$, are not associated with any Nodes -\/-\/ instead,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01951}01951 they represent "{}internal"{} data for each individual element.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01952}01952 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01953}01953 <B>Implementation</B> \(\backslash\)n\(\backslash\)n}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01954}01954 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01955}01955 To facilitate the implementation of discontinuous interpolations}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01956}01956 we introduce two modifications to our data structure:}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01957}01957 -\/\# We split the \(\backslash\)c Node class into two separate classes:}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01958}01958    -\/ The base class \(\backslash\)c Data which contains only the "{}values"{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01959}01959      and their global equation numbers.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01960}01960    -\/ The derived class \(\backslash\)c Node which inherits from \(\backslash\)c Data and}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01961}01961      adds the additional functionality that is required by actual Nodes}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01962}01962      (storage for the Eulerian coordinates and the associated }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01963}01963      access functions).}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01964}01964 -\/\# Each FiniteElement provides storage for "{}Internal Data"{} in}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01965}01965    a vector of (pointers to) \(\backslash\)c Data objects. By default, the }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01966}01966    vector of "{}Internal}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01967}01967    Data"{} is a vector of zero length. Specific FiniteElements}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01968}01968    can resize this vector in their constructor to provide a sufficient}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01969}01969    amount of storage for their Internal Data (if they require any).}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01970}01970    Internal Data is included in the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01971}01971    global equation numbering procedure by providing }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01972}01972    the function \(\backslash\)c FiniteElement::assign\_internal\_eqn\_numbers()}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01973}01973    which allocates distinct global equation numbers to all values}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01974}01974    that are stored in the element's "{}Internal Data"{}. the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01975}01975    function is executed for each element when the global equation }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01976}01976    numbers are assigned by \(\backslash\)c Problem::assign\_eqn\_numbers(). }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01977}01977 .}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01978}01978 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01979}01979 <HR>}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01980}01980 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01981}01981 \(\backslash\)subsection higher\_order\_pdes Higher-\/order PDEs -\/-\/ Hermite interpolants}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01982}01982 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01983}01983 All the examples considered so far involved second-\/order PDEs}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01984}01984 whose weak form could be integrated by parts. Therefore we only needed}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01985}01985 to evaluate integrals that involve first derivatives}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01986}01986 of the basis functions. Such integrals can be evaluated}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01987}01987 for basis functions that are globally continuous but have}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01988}01988 e.g. discontinuous first derivatives at isolated points (at the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01989}01989 element boundaries). The piecewise}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01990}01990 linear/quadratic/... (global) finite-\/element shape functions }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01991}01991 introduced in section \(\backslash\)ref fe\_basis\_fct}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01992}01992 satisfied these criteria. Since these representation of the function}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01993}01993 with these shape functions implements a (Lagrange) interpolation }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01994}01994 between the nodal values, such finite elements are often referred}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01995}01995 to as Lagrange finite elements. }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01996}01996 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01997}01997 Let us now consider the fourth-\/order problem }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01998}01998 \(\backslash\)f[ \(\backslash\)frac\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\}\string^4 u(x)\}\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\} x\string^4\} = f(x)  \(\backslash\)mbox\{ \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l01999}01999 for \$x\(\backslash\)in[0,1]\$\(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) (1)\}  \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02000}02000 subject to the essential boundary conditions}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02001}02001 \(\backslash\)f[ u(0)=g\_0, \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)  u(1)=g\_1, \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02002}02002 \(\backslash\)left. \(\backslash\)frac\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\}u\}\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\}x\}\(\backslash\)right|\_\{x=0\}=h\_0, \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)  }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02003}02003 \(\backslash\)left.\(\backslash\)frac\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\}u\}\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\}x\}\(\backslash\)right|\_\{x=1\}=h\_1,\(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02004}02004 where \(\backslash\)f\$f(x)\(\backslash\)f\$ and the constants \(\backslash\)f\$g\_0,g\_1,h\_0\(\backslash\)f\$ and \(\backslash\)f\$h\_1\(\backslash\)f\$ are}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02005}02005 given. }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02006}02006 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02007}02007 We define the weak form of (1) by requiring that the (weak) solution}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02008}02008 satisfies the essential boundary conditions and that the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02009}02009 weighted residual}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02010}02010 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02011}02011 r = \(\backslash\)int\_0\string^1  \(\backslash\)left( \(\backslash\)frac\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\}\string^4 u(x)\}\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\} x\string^4\} -\/ f(x) \(\backslash\)right)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02012}02012  \(\backslash\)phi\string^\{(test)\}(x) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)mbox\{d\}x \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) (2)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02013}02013 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02014}02014 vanishes for all test functions  \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)phi\string^\{(test)\}(x) \(\backslash\)f\$ which satisfy}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02015}02015 the homogeneous boundary conditions}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02016}02016 \(\backslash\)f[ \(\backslash\)phi\string^\{(test)\}(0)=0, \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)  \(\backslash\)phi\string^\{(test)\}(1)=0, \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02017}02017 \(\backslash\)left. \(\backslash\)frac\{d\(\backslash\)phi\string^\{(test)\}\}\{dx\}\(\backslash\)right|\_\{x=0\}=0, \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)  }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02018}02018 \(\backslash\)left.\(\backslash\)frac\{d\(\backslash\)phi\string^\{(test)\}\}\{dx\}\(\backslash\)right|\_\{x=1\}=0.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02019}02019 \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) (3) \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02020}02020 We can integrate the weak form (2) twice by parts to obtain}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02021}02021 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02022}02022 r = \(\backslash\)int\_0\string^1  \(\backslash\)left(}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02023}02023     \(\backslash\)frac\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\}\string^2 u(x)\}\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\} x\string^2\} }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02024}02024     \(\backslash\)frac\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\}\string^2 \(\backslash\)phi\string^\{(test)\}(x)\}\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\} x\string^2\}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02025}02025      -\/ f(x) \(\backslash\)phi\string^\{(test)\}(x) \(\backslash\)right) \(\backslash\) dx}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02026}02026    \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)  + \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)left[ \(\backslash\)left. \(\backslash\)frac\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\}\string^3 u(x)\}\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\} x\string^3\} }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02027}02027               \(\backslash\)phi\string^\{(test)\}(x) \(\backslash\)right] \(\backslash\)right|\_\{0\}\string^1}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02028}02028    \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)  -\/ \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)left[ \(\backslash\)left. \(\backslash\)frac\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\}\string^2 u(x)\}\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\} x\string^2\}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02029}02029        \(\backslash\)frac\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\} \(\backslash\)phi\string^\{(test)\}(x)\}\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\} x\} \(\backslash\)right]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02030}02030       \(\backslash\)right|\_\{0\}\string^1.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02031}02031 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02032}02032 As before, the boundary terms vanish because \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)phi\string^\{(test)\}(x)\(\backslash\)f\$  }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02033}02033 satisfies the homogeneous boundary conditions (3), and we obtain}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02034}02034 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02035}02035 r = \(\backslash\)int\_0\string^1  \(\backslash\)left(}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02036}02036     \(\backslash\)frac\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\}\string^2 u(x)\}\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\} x\string^2\} }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02037}02037     \(\backslash\)frac\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\}\string^2 \(\backslash\)phi\string^\{(test)\}(x)\}\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\} x\string^2\}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02038}02038      -\/ f(x) \(\backslash\)phi\string^\{(test)\}(x) \(\backslash\)right) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)mbox\{d\}x \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) (4).}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02039}02039 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02040}02040 We now follow the usual (Galerkin) procedure of}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02041}02041 expanding the solution \(\backslash\)f\$ u(x) \(\backslash\)f\$ and the test function }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02042}02042 \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)phi\string^\{(test)\}(x)\(\backslash\)f\$ in terms of}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02043}02043 the same set of basis functions \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)psi\_j(x)\(\backslash\)f\$. The integral (4) shows}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02044}02044 that the basis functions now}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02045}02045 need to have square-\/integrable second derivatives, i.e. }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02046}02046 we have to require that \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)psi\_j(x) \(\backslash\)in H\string^2\_0(D)\(\backslash\)f\$ rather}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02047}02047 than  \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)psi\_j(x) \(\backslash\)in H\string^1\_0(D)\(\backslash\)f\$ as in the case of the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02048}02048 second-\/order problem P1. }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02049}02049 The Lagrange interpolants that are generated by piecewise}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02050}02050 linear or quadratic finite element shape functions are not members}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02051}02051 of  \(\backslash\)f\$ H\string^2\_0(D)\(\backslash\)f\$ because their first derivatives are discontinuous between}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02052}02052 elements. }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02053}02053 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02054}02054 Basis functions of sufficient differentiability can be}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02055}02055 constructed by Hermite interpolation. For this  purpose we introduce}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02056}02056 two different types of basis functions:}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02057}02057 -\/ Basis functions of type 1 provide an interpolation between the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02058}02058   nodal values and thus satisfy the conditions}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02059}02059   \(\backslash\)f[ \(\backslash\)psi\_\{j1\}(X\_k) = \(\backslash\)delta\_\{jk\}, \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02060}02060   implying that they are equal to one at exactly \(\backslash\)e one node while they }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02061}02061   vanish at all others. Furthermore, these basis functions satisfy}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02062}02062   \(\backslash\)f[ \(\backslash\)left. \(\backslash\)frac\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\}\(\backslash\)psi\_\{j1\}\}\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\}x\} \(\backslash\)right|\_\{X\_k\} = 0 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02063}02063   \(\backslash\)mbox\{\(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) for \$j,k=1,...,N\$\}, \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02064}02064   so that their derivatives vanish at \(\backslash\)e all nodal points.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02065}02065 -\/ Basis functions of type 2 provide an independent interpolation}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02066}02066   for the derivatives of the function and thus satisfy the conditions}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02067}02067   \(\backslash\)f[ \(\backslash\)left. \(\backslash\)frac\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\}\(\backslash\)psi\_\{j2\}\}\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\}x\} \(\backslash\)right|\_\{X\_k\} = \(\backslash\)delta\_\{jk\} , \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02068}02068   implying that their derivative is equal to one at exactly }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02069}02069   \(\backslash\)e one nodal point and zero at all others. Furthermore, these}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02070}02070   basis functions satisfy}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02071}02071   \(\backslash\)f[ \(\backslash\)psi\_\{j2\}(X\_k) = 0 \(\backslash\)mbox\{\(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) for \$j,k=1,...,N\$\}, \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02072}02072   so that they vanish at \(\backslash\)e all nodal points.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02073}02073 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02074}02074 The global Hermite shape functions are illustrated in this sketch:}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02075}02075 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02076}02076 \(\backslash\)image html 1Dmesh\_with\_hermite\_shape\_fcts.gif "{}1D Hermite shape "{} }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02077}02077 \(\backslash\)image latex 1Dmesh\_with\_hermite\_shape\_fcts.eps "{}1D Hermite shape "{} width=0.75\(\backslash\)textwidth}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02078}02078 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02079}02079 The global Hermite shape functions have local equivalents which are}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02080}02080 again expressed in terms of a local coordinate \(\backslash\)f\$s \(\backslash\)in [0,1]\(\backslash\)f\$}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02081}02081 (note that the coordinate range differs from that for the Lagrange }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02082}02082 elements) as}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02083}02083 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02084}02084 \(\backslash\)todo ***ANDREW SHOULD WE CHANGE THE RANGE TO [-\/1,1] ?? ***}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02085}02085 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02086}02086 \(\backslash\)f[ \(\backslash\)psi\_\{11\}(s) =  2s\string^3 -\/ 3s\string^2 + 1 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02087}02087 \(\backslash\)f[ \(\backslash\)psi\_\{12\}(s) = s\string^3 -\/ 2s\string^2 + s \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02088}02088 \(\backslash\)f[ \(\backslash\)psi\_\{21\}(s) = 3s\string^2 -\/ 2s\string^3 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02089}02089 \(\backslash\)f[ \(\backslash\)psi\_\{22\}(s) = s\string^3 -\/ s\string^2. \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02090}02090 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02091}02091 The shape functions for [-\/1,1] are}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02092}02092 \(\backslash\)f[ \(\backslash\)psi\_\{11\}(s) =  \(\backslash\)frac\{1\}\{4\}\(\backslash\)left(s\string^3 -\/ 3s + 2\(\backslash\)right) \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02093}02093 \(\backslash\)f[ \(\backslash\)psi\_\{12\}(s) = \(\backslash\)frac\{1\}\{4\}\(\backslash\)left(s\string^3 -\/ s\string^2 -\/ s + 1 \(\backslash\)right) \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02094}02094 \(\backslash\)f[ \(\backslash\)psi\_\{21\}(s) = \(\backslash\)frac\{1\}\{4\}\(\backslash\)left(2 + 3s -\/ s\string^3\(\backslash\)right) \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02095}02095 \(\backslash\)f[ \(\backslash\)psi\_\{22\}(s) = \(\backslash\)frac\{1\}\{4\}\(\backslash\)left(s\string^3 + s\string^2 -\/ s -\/ 1\(\backslash\)right). \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02096}02096 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02097}02097 Using these shape functions we can represent the unknown function \(\backslash\)f\$ u \(\backslash\)f\$ }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02098}02098 in element \(\backslash\)f\$e\(\backslash\)f\$ as}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02099}02099 \(\backslash\)f[ u = \(\backslash\)sum\_\{j=1\}\string^2  \(\backslash\)sum\_\{k=1\}\string^2 U\_\{\{\(\backslash\)cal J\}(j,e)k\}\(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)psi\_\{jk\}(s), \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02100}02100 where each node now stores two "{}types"{} of degree of freedom: \(\backslash\)f\$U\_\{j1\} \(\backslash\)f\$}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02101}02101 represents the nodal value at node \(\backslash\)f\$ j \(\backslash\)f\$ and  \(\backslash\)f\$U\_\{j2\} \(\backslash\)f\$ represents}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02102}02102 (a measure of) the derivative of the function at that node.  }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02103}02103 In isoparametric elements, }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02104}02104 the same shape functions are used to represent the mapping }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02105}02105 between \(\backslash\)f\$x\(\backslash\)f\$ and \(\backslash\)f\$ s\(\backslash\)f\$ so we have}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02106}02106 \(\backslash\)f[ x(s) = \(\backslash\)sum\_\{j=1\}\string^2  \(\backslash\)sum\_\{k=1\}\string^2 X\_\{\{\(\backslash\)cal J\}(j,e)k\}\(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)psi\_\{jk\}(s). \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02107}02107 Here  \(\backslash\)f\$X\_\{j1\} \(\backslash\)f\$ represents the \(\backslash\)f\$x\(\backslash\)f\$ coordinate of nodal point}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02108}02108 \(\backslash\)f\$j\(\backslash\)f\$. We refer to the coefficients \(\backslash\)f\$X\_\{j2\} \(\backslash\)f\$ as "{}generalised}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02109}02109 coordinates"{}. During the mesh-\/generation process the values of}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02110}02110 these generalised coordinates must be chosen such that the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02111}02111 mapping \(\backslash\)f\$ x(s)\(\backslash\)f\$ is one-\/to-\/one over the entire element.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02112}02112 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02113}02113 <HR>}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02114}02114 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02115}02115 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02116}02116 \(\backslash\)subsection hyperbol\_parabol\_timestep Parabolic and hyperbolic problems -\/-\/ timestepping}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02117}02117 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02118}02118 The PDEs discussed so far were all of elliptic type. However,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02119}02119 the finite element method can also be used for the (semi-\/)discretisation}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02120}02120 of parabolic and hyperbolic problems. We will demonstrate}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02121}02121 this by considering the two classical examples of}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02122}02122 these equations: i) the unsteady heat equation and ii) the wave equation.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02123}02123 \(\backslash\)subsubsection unsteady\_heat The unsteady heat equation}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02124}02124 The 2D unsteady heat equation is given by }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02125}02125 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02126}02126 \(\backslash\)sum\_\{k=1\}\string^2 \(\backslash\)frac\{\(\backslash\)partial\string^2 u(x\_i,t)\}\{\(\backslash\)partial x\_k\string^2\} }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02127}02127 = \(\backslash\)frac\{\(\backslash\)partial u(x\_i,t)\}\{\(\backslash\)partial t\} + f(x\_i,t)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02128}02128 \(\backslash\)mbox\{\(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) in \$D\$\}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02129}02129 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02130}02130 subject to the boundary condition}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02131}02131 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02132}02132 u\(\backslash\)left(x\_i\string^\{\(\backslash\)partial D\}(\(\backslash\)zeta),t\(\backslash\)right) = g(\(\backslash\)zeta,t) }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02133}02133 \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) (12)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02134}02134 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02135}02135 and the initial condition}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02136}02136 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02137}02137 u(x\_i,t=t\_0) = u\string^\{(IC)\}(x\_i), \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) (13)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02138}02138 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02139}02139 for the given functions \(\backslash\)f\$ f(x\_i,t), \(\backslash\) g(\(\backslash\)zeta,t) \(\backslash\)f\$}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02140}02140 and \(\backslash\)f\$ u\string^\{(IC)\}(x\_i)\(\backslash\)f\$.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02141}02141 Superficially, the only difference between this parabolic problem}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02142}02142 and the elliptic Poisson problem P2 is the presence of the }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02143}02143 time-\/derivative on the RHS of the PDE and the fact that the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02144}02144 boundary conditions and the source function are time-\/dependent. }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02145}02145 Motivated by this observation, we employ the same spatial discretisation}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02146}02146 as in the Poisson problem by writing}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02147}02147 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02148}02148 u(x\_i,t) = \(\backslash\)sum\_\{j=1\}\string^N U\_j(t) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)psi\_j(x\_i)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02149}02149 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02150}02150 where the coefficients  \(\backslash\)f\$ U\_j(t) \(\backslash\)f\$ are now}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02151}02151 (continuous) functions of time \(\backslash\)f\$ t \(\backslash\)f\$. Following the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02152}02152 usual procedures, we obtain the residuals}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02153}02153 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02154}02154 r\_l(t) = \(\backslash\)int\_D \(\backslash\)left[ \(\backslash\)sum\_\{j=1\}\string^N \(\backslash\)left( U\_j(t) }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02155}02155 \(\backslash\)sum\_\{k=1\}\string^2}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02156}02156 \(\backslash\)frac\{\(\backslash\)partial \(\backslash\)psi\_j(x\_i)\}\{\(\backslash\)partial x\_k\} }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02157}02157 \(\backslash\)frac\{\(\backslash\)partial \(\backslash\)psi\_l(x\_i)\}\{\(\backslash\)partial x\_k\} +}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02158}02158 \(\backslash\)frac\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\} U\_j(t)\}\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\} t\} \(\backslash\)psi\_j(x\_i) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)psi\_l(x\_i) \(\backslash\)right) +}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02159}02159 f(x\_i,t) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)psi\_l(x\_i) \(\backslash\)right] \(\backslash\)mbox\{d\}x\_1 \(\backslash\)mbox\{d\}x\_2 = 0 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02160}02160 \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) (14)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02161}02161 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02162}02162 for all coefficients \(\backslash\)f\$ U\_l(t) \(\backslash\)f\$ whose values are not determined}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02163}02163 by the boundary conditions. The residuals now form}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02164}02164 a system of ODEs, rather than a system of algebraic equations -\/-\/}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02165}02165 the spatial discretisation has only achieved a semi-\/discretisation.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02166}02166 We obtain the initial conditions for the unknown coefficients }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02167}02167 \(\backslash\)f\$ U\_l(t) \(\backslash\)f\$ by evaluating (13) at the nodal}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02168}02168 positions}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02169}02169 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02170}02170 U\_j(t=t\_0) = u\string^\{(IC)\}(X\_\{ij\})}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02171}02171 \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) (15)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02172}02172 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02173}02173 The solution of the initial-\/value problem defined by}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02174}02174 the system of first-\/order ODEs (14) and the }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02175}02175 initial conditions (15) can now be obtained by}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02176}02176 any ODE solver. Within \(\backslash\)c oomph-\/lib we provide the implicit }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02177}02177 timesteppers from the BDF family as the default}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02178}02178 timesteppers for parabolic problems. In these schemes,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02179}02179 the time-\/derivatives are approximated by}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02180}02180 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02181}02181 \(\backslash\)frac\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\} U\_j\}\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\} t\} \(\backslash\)approx }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02182}02182 \(\backslash\)sum\_\{\(\backslash\)tau=0\}\string^\{N\_\{history\}\}  \(\backslash\)left.\string^\(\backslash\)tau U\_j\(\backslash\)right.  \(\backslash\)left.\string^\(\backslash\)tau W\(\backslash\)right.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02183}02183 \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)  (16)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02184}02184 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02185}02185 where the values \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)left.\string^\(\backslash\)tau U\_j\(\backslash\)right. \(\backslash\)f\$  represent}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02186}02186 the history of the nodal value \(\backslash\)f\$  U\_j \(\backslash\)f\$, i.e. its values}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02187}02187 at current and previous (discrete) timesteps. }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02188}02188 If the time-\/integration is performed with a constant timestep}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02189}02189  \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)Delta t \(\backslash\)f\$, we have}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02190}02190 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02191}02191  \(\backslash\)left.\string^\(\backslash\)tau U\_j\(\backslash\)right. =  U\_j(t-\/\(\backslash\)tau \(\backslash\)Delta t)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02192}02192 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02193}02193 so \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)left.\string^0 U\_j\(\backslash\)right. \(\backslash\)f\$}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02194}02194 represents the (unknown) nodal value at the present time.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02195}02195 The weights \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)left.\string^\(\backslash\)tau W\(\backslash\)right. \(\backslash\)f\$ are constants that depend}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02196}02196 only on the timestep \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)Delta t\(\backslash\)f\$.  And, yes, }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02197}02197 the \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)tau \(\backslash\)f\$ is a left superscript.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02198}02198 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02199}02199 The different members of the BDF family are distinguished by the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02200}02200 number of previous values used in the approximation (16).}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02201}02201 For the BDF1 scheme we have \(\backslash\)f\$ N\_\{history\}=1\(\backslash\)f\$ with the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02202}02202 weights}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02203}02203 \(\backslash\)f[  }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02204}02204 \(\backslash\)left.\string^0 W\(\backslash\)right. = \(\backslash\)frac\{1\}\{\(\backslash\)Delta t\} \(\backslash\)mbox\{\(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) and \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02205}02205 \(\backslash\)left.\string^1 W\(\backslash\)right. = -\/ \(\backslash\)frac\{1\}\{\(\backslash\)Delta t\}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02206}02206 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02207}02207 Inserting the weights into (16), we recover the }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02208}02208 classical first-\/order-\/accurate backward Euler scheme:}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02209}02209 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02210}02210 \(\backslash\)frac\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\} U\_j\}\{\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\} t\} \(\backslash\)approx }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02211}02211 \(\backslash\)frac\{ \(\backslash\)left.\string^0 U\_j\(\backslash\)right. -\/  \(\backslash\)left.\string^1 U\_j\(\backslash\)right. \}\{\(\backslash\)Delta t\}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02212}02212 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02213}02213 Similarly, in the BDF2 scheme we have \(\backslash\)f\$ N\_\{history\}=2\(\backslash\)f\$ with the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02214}02214 weights}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02215}02215 \(\backslash\)f[  }

\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02295}02295 \(\backslash\)subsubsection timestep\_implementation Implementation}

\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02301}02301 \(\backslash\)subsection solids\_lagrange Solid mechanics problems -\/-\/ Lagrangian coordinates}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02302}02302 All problems discussed so far were formulated in an Eulerian frame,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02303}02303 i.e. we assumed all unknowns to be functions of the spatially-\/fixed,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02304}02304 Eulerian coordinates, \(\backslash\)f\$x\_i \(\backslash\) (i=1,...,3)\(\backslash\)f\$, and of time, }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02305}02305 \(\backslash\)f\$ t \(\backslash\)f\$. Many problems }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02306}02306 in solid mechanics are formulated more conveniently in terms of }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02307}02307 body-\/attached, Lagrangian coordinates. In this section we will}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02308}02308 briefly review the essential concepts of nonlinear continuum mechanics}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02309}02309 and present the principle of virtual displacements which forms the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02310}02310 basis for all large-\/displacement solid mechanics computations in \(\backslash\)c oomph-\/lib.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02311}02311 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02312}02312 Throughout this section we will use the summation convention }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02313}02313 so that repeated indices are assumed to be summed over the range}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02314}02314 of the three spatial coordinates and all free indices range }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02315}02315 from 1 to 3. We will retain the summation signs}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02316}02316 for all other sums, such as sums over the nodes etc.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02317}02317 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02318}02318 \(\backslash\)subsubsection geometry The geometry}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02319}02319 The figure below introduces the essential geometrical concepts: }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02320}02320 We employ a set of Lagrangian coordinates, \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)xi\string^i\(\backslash\)f\$, to}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02321}02321 parametrise the (Eulerian) position vector to material points in the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02322}02322  body's undeformed position:}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02323}02323 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02324}02324 \{\(\backslash\)bf r\} = \{\(\backslash\)bf r\}(\(\backslash\)xi\string^i).}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02325}02325 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02326}02326 The specific choice of the Lagrangian coordinates is }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02327}02327 irrelevant for the subsequent development. For analytical studies, it is}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02328}02328 advantageous to choose a body-\/fitted Lagrangian coordinate}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02329}02329 system (as shown in the sketch) because this allows boundary}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02330}02330 conditions to be applied on iso-\/levels of the coordinates;}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02331}02331 in computational studies, it is usually preferable to use a }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02332}02332 coordinate system in which the governing equations are as compact}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02333}02333 as possible. A cartesian coordinate system is best suited for this }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02334}02334 purpose.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02335}02335 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02336}02336 We denote the tangent vectors to the coordinate lines \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)xi\string^i = const.\(\backslash\)f\$}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02337}02337 in the undeformed configuration by}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02338}02338 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02339}02339 \{\(\backslash\)bf g\}\_i = \(\backslash\)frac\{\(\backslash\)partial \{\(\backslash\)bf r\}\}\{\(\backslash\)partial \(\backslash\)xi\string^i\}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02340}02340 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02341}02341 and define the components of the covariant metric tensor via }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02342}02342 the inner products}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02343}02343 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02344}02344 g\_\{ij\} = \{\(\backslash\)bf g\}\_i \(\backslash\)cdot \{\(\backslash\)bf g\}\_j.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02345}02345 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02346}02346 This tensor defines the "{}metric"{} because the (square of the) infinitesimal }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02347}02347 length, \(\backslash\)f\$ ds \(\backslash\)f\$, of a line element with coordinate increments }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02348}02348 \(\backslash\)f\$ d\(\backslash\)xi\string^i\(\backslash\)f\$ is given by}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02349}02349 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02350}02350 (ds)\string^2 = g\_\{ij\} \(\backslash\)  d\(\backslash\)xi\string^i d\(\backslash\)xi\string^j.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02351}02351 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02352}02352 The volume of the infinitesimal parallelepiped formed by}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02353}02353 the coordinate increments  \(\backslash\)f\$ d\(\backslash\)xi\string^i\(\backslash\)f\$ is given by}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02354}02354 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02355}02355 dv = \(\backslash\)sqrt\{g\} \(\backslash\) d\(\backslash\)xi\string^1 d\(\backslash\)xi\string^2 d\(\backslash\)xi\string^3,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02356}02356 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02357}02357 where }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02358}02358 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02359}02359 g = \(\backslash\)det g\_\{ij\}. }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02360}02360 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02361}02361  }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02362}02362 \(\backslash\)image html Lagrangian\_coord.gif "{}2D sketch of the Lagrangian coordinates. The Lagrangian coordinates parametrise the position vector to material points in the body. As the body deforms, the Lagrangian coordinates remain attached to the same material points and the coordinate lines become distorted. The change in the length of infinitesimal material line elements provides an objective measure of the body's "{} }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02363}02363 \(\backslash\)image latex Lagrangian\_coord.eps "{}2D sketch of the Lagrangian coordinates. The Lagrangian coordinates parametrise the position vector to material points in the body. The change in the length of infinitesimal material line elements provides an objective measure of the body's "{} width=0.75\(\backslash\)textwidth}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02364}02364 As the body deforms, the Lagrangian coordinates remain "{}attached"{} to the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02365}02365 same material points. The body's deformation can therefore be}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02366}02366 described bt the vector field that specifies the position vectors }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02367}02367 to material particles in the deformed configuration,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02368}02368 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02369}02369 \{\(\backslash\)bf R\} = \{\(\backslash\)bf R\}(\(\backslash\)xi\string^i).}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02370}02370 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02371}02371 As in the undeformed coordinate system, we  form the }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02372}02372 tangent vectors to the deformed coordinate lines \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)xi\string^i = const.\(\backslash\)f\$}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02373}02373 and denote them by}
