\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02523}02523    (22).}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02524}02524    Given the deformed and undeformed metric tensors,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02525}02525    the computation of the stress tensor \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)sigma\string^\{ij\} \(\backslash\)f\$ }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02526}02526    for an incompressible}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02527}02527    material therefore requires the computation of the following quantities:}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02528}02528    -\/ The deviatoric stress \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)overline\{\(\backslash\)sigma\}\string^\{ij\} \(\backslash\)f\$}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02529}02529    -\/ The contravariant deformed metric tensor  \(\backslash\)f\$ G\string^\{ij\} \(\backslash\)f\$}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02530}02530    -\/ The determinant of the deformed }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02531}02531      metric tensor \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)det G\_\{ij\} \(\backslash\)f\$ which }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02532}02532      is required in equation (22)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02533}02533      whose solution determines the pressure.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02534}02534    .}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02535}02535   \(\backslash\)n}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02536}02536 -\/\# \(\backslash\)b Nearly \(\backslash\)b Incompressible \(\backslash\)b Behaviour: \(\backslash\)n If the material is nearly}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02537}02537    incompressible, it is advantageous to split the stress into}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02538}02538    its deviatoric and hydrostatic parts by writing the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02539}02539    constitutive law in the form}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02540}02540    \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02541}02541    \(\backslash\)sigma\string^\{ij\} = -\/p G\string^\{ij\} + }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02542}02542    \(\backslash\)overline\{\(\backslash\)sigma\}\string^\{ij\}\(\backslash\)big(\(\backslash\)gamma\_\{kl\}\(\backslash\)big),}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02543}02543    \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) (24)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02544}02544    \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02545}02545    where the deviatoric part of the stress tensor, }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02546}02546    \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)overline\{\(\backslash\)sigma\}\string^\{ij\}, \(\backslash\)f\$ depends on the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02547}02547    strain. This form of the constitutive}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02548}02548    law is identical to that of the incompressible}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02549}02549    case and it involves a pressure \(\backslash\)f\$ p \(\backslash\)f\$ which needs to be}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02550}02550    determined from an additional equation. In the }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02551}02551    incompressible case, this equation was given by the incompressibility}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02552}02552    constraint (22). Here, we need to augment }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02553}02553    the constitutive law for the deviatoric stress by}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02554}02554    an additional equation for the pressure. Generally this takes the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02555}02555    form}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02556}02556    \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02557}02557    p = \(\backslash\)kappa \(\backslash\) d}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02558}02558    \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) (25)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02559}02559    \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02560}02560    where \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)kappa \(\backslash\)f\$ is the "{}bulk modulus"{}, a material property}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02561}02561    that needs to be specified by the constitutive law.   }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02562}02562    \(\backslash\)f\$ d \(\backslash\)f\$ is the (generalised) dilatation, i.e. the relative change}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02563}02563    in the volume of an infinitesimal material element (or some}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02564}02564    suitable generalised quantity that is related to it). As the }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02565}02565    material approaches incompressibility, \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)kappa \(\backslash\)to \(\backslash\)infty\(\backslash\)f\$, so that}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02566}02566    infinitely large pressures would be required to achieve}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02567}02567    any change in volume. To facilitate the implementation of}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02568}02568    (25) as the equation for the pressure, we re-\/write }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02569}02569    it in the form}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02570}02570    \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02571}02571    p \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)frac\{1\}\{\(\backslash\)kappa\} -\/  d\(\backslash\)big(g\_\{ij\},G\_\{ij\}\(\backslash\)big) = 0}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02572}02572    \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) (26) }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02573}02573    \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02574}02574    which only involves quantities that remain finite }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02575}02575    as we approach true incompressibility.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02576}02576    \(\backslash\)n }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02577}02577    Given the deformed and undeformed metric tensors,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02578}02578    the computation of the stress tensor \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)sigma\string^\{ij\} \(\backslash\)f\$ }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02579}02579    for a nearly incompressible}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02580}02580    material therefore requires the computation of the following quantities:}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02581}02581    -\/ The deviatoric stress \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)overline\{\(\backslash\)sigma\}\string^\{ij\} \(\backslash\)f\$}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02582}02582    -\/ The contravariant deformed metric tensor  \(\backslash\)f\$ G\string^\{ij\} \(\backslash\)f\$}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02583}02583    -\/ The generalised dilatation \(\backslash\)f\$ d \(\backslash\)f\$}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02584}02584    -\/ The inverse of the bulk modulus \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)kappa \(\backslash\)f\$}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02585}02585    .}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02586}02586   \(\backslash\)n}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02587}02587 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02588}02588 The abstract base class \(\backslash\)c ConstitutiveLaw provides}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02589}02589 interfaces for the computation of the stress in all three forms.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02590}02590 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02591}02591 \(\backslash\)subsubsection non-\/dim\_solid Non-\/dimensionalisation}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02592}02592 The principle of virtual displacements (20)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02593}02593 is written in dimensional form.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02594}02594 We generally prefer to work with non-\/dimensional quantities and}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02595}02595 will now discuss the non-\/dimensionalisation used in the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02596}02596 actual implementation of the equations in \(\backslash\)c oomph-\/lib. For this purpose we }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02597}02597 first re-\/write equation (20) as}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02598}02598 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02599}02599 \(\backslash\)int\_\{v\} \(\backslash\)left\(\backslash\)\{ \(\backslash\)sigma\string^\{*ij\} \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)delta \(\backslash\)gamma\_\{ij\} -\/  \(\backslash\)left( \{\(\backslash\)bf f\}\string^* -\/ }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02600}02600  \(\backslash\)rho \(\backslash\)frac\{\(\backslash\)partial\string^2 \{\(\backslash\)bf R\}\string^*\}\{\(\backslash\)partial t\string^\{*2\}\} \(\backslash\)right) \(\backslash\)cdot }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02601}02601  \(\backslash\)delta \{\(\backslash\)bf R\}\string^* \(\backslash\)right\(\backslash\)\} \(\backslash\) dv\string^* }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02602}02602  -\/ \(\backslash\)oint\_\{A\_\{tract\}\} \{\(\backslash\)bf t\}\string^* \(\backslash\)cdot \(\backslash\)delta \{\(\backslash\)bf R\}\string^* \(\backslash\) dA\string^* =0,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02603}02603   \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) (27)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02604}02604  \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02605}02605 where have used asterisks to label those}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02606}02606 dimensional quantities that will have non-\/dimensional equivalents.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02607}02607 (Some quantities, such as the strain, are already}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02608}02608 dimensionless, while others, such as the density will not have}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02609}02609 any non-\/dimensional counterparts. We do not introduce modifiers}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02610}02610 for these).}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02611}02611 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02612}02612 We now non-\/dimensionalise all lengths with a problem-\/specific}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02613}02613 length-\/scale, \(\backslash\)f\$ \{\(\backslash\)cal L\}\(\backslash\)f\$, given e.g. the length of the solid}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02614}02614 body, so that}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02615}02615 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02616}02616 \(\backslash\)xi\string^\{*i\} = \{\(\backslash\)cal L\} \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)xi\string^\{i\}, \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)  \{\(\backslash\)bf R\}\string^* = \{\(\backslash\)cal L\} \(\backslash\) \{\(\backslash\)bf R\}, }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02617}02617 \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) dA\string^* = \{\(\backslash\)cal L\}\string^2 \(\backslash\) dA, \(\backslash\)mbox\{ \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) and \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \} }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02618}02618 dv\string^* = \{\(\backslash\)cal L\}\string^3 \(\backslash\) dv.\(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02619}02619 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02620}02620 We use a characteristic stiffness, \(\backslash\)f\$ \{\(\backslash\)cal S\}\(\backslash\)f\$, (e.g. the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02621}02621 material's Young's modulus \(\backslash\)f\$ E \(\backslash\)f\$) to non-\/dimensionalise}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02622}02622 the stress and the loads as}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02623}02623 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02624}02624 \(\backslash\)sigma\string^\{*ij\} = \{\(\backslash\)cal S\} \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)sigma\string^\{ij\}, \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)  \{\(\backslash\)bf t\}\string^* = \{\(\backslash\)cal S\}\(\backslash\)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02625}02625 \{\(\backslash\)bf t\}, \(\backslash\)mbox\{ \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) and \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \} \{\(\backslash\)bf f\}\string^* = \{\(\backslash\)cal S\} / \{\(\backslash\)cal L\} \(\backslash\)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02626}02626 \{\(\backslash\)bf f\},}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02627}02627 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02628}02628 and we non-\/dimensionalise time with a problem-\/specific}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02629}02629 timescale \(\backslash\)f\$ \{\(\backslash\)cal T\}\(\backslash\)f\$ (e.g. the period of some external forcing),}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02630}02630 so that}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02631}02631 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02632}02632 t\string^* = \{\(\backslash\)cal T\} t.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02633}02633 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02634}02634 This transforms (27) into}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02635}02635 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02636}02636 \(\backslash\)int\_\{v\} \(\backslash\)left\(\backslash\)\{ \(\backslash\)sigma\string^\{ij\} \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)delta \(\backslash\)gamma\_\{ij\} -\/ \(\backslash\)left( \{\(\backslash\)bf f\} -\/ }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02637}02637  \(\backslash\)Lambda\string^2 \(\backslash\)frac\{\(\backslash\)partial\string^2 \{\(\backslash\)bf R\}\}\{\(\backslash\)partial t\string^\{2\}\} \(\backslash\)right) \(\backslash\)cdot }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02638}02638  \(\backslash\)delta \{\(\backslash\)bf R\} \(\backslash\)right\(\backslash\)\} \(\backslash\) dv }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02639}02639  -\/\(\backslash\)oint\_\{A\_\{tract\}\} \{\(\backslash\)bf t\} \(\backslash\)cdot \(\backslash\)delta \{\(\backslash\)bf R\} \(\backslash\) dA =0,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02640}02640   \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) (28)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02641}02641  \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02642}02642  where }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02643}02643 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02644}02644 \(\backslash\)Lambda = \(\backslash\)frac\{1\}\{\(\backslash\)cal T\} \(\backslash\)sqrt\{\(\backslash\)frac\{\(\backslash\)rho \{\(\backslash\)cal L\}\}\{\(\backslash\)cal S\}\}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02645}02645 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02646}02646 is the ratio of system's "{}intrinsic"{} timescale, }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02647}02647 \(\backslash\)f\$T\_\{intrinsic\} = \(\backslash\)sqrt\{\(\backslash\)rho \{\(\backslash\)cal L\}/\{\(\backslash\)cal S\}\},\(\backslash\)f\$ to the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02648}02648 time, \(\backslash\)f\$\{\(\backslash\)cal T\}\(\backslash\)f\$, used in the non-\/dimensionalisation of the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02649}02649 equations. If a given problem has no externally imposed timescale}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02650}02650 (e.g. in the free vibrations of an elastic body) \(\backslash\)f\$T\_\{intrinsic\}\(\backslash\)f\$}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02651}02651 (or some suitable problem-\/dependent multiple thereof) provides a natural }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02652}02652 timescale for the non-\/dimensionalisation. Therefore we use }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02653}02653 \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)Lambda=1 \(\backslash\)f\$ as the default value in all solid mechanics}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02654}02654 equations. If preferred, computations can, of course, be}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02655}02655 be performed with dimensional units, provided all quantities}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02656}02656 are expressed in consistent units (e.g. from the SI system).}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02657}02657 In this case \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)Lambda\string^2 \(\backslash\)f\$ represents the dimensional}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02658}02658 density of the material.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02659}02659 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02660}02660 We adopt a similar approach for non-\/dimensionalisation of the }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02661}02661 constitutive equations. Typically, the constitutive parameters}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02662}02662 (e.g. Young's modulus and Poisson's ratio for a Hookean}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02663}02663 constitutive equation) are passed to the \(\backslash\)c ConstitutiveLaw}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02664}02664 as arguments to its constructor. Where possible, we select one of these}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02665}02665 parameters as the reference stress \(\backslash\)f\$ \{\(\backslash\)cal S\} \(\backslash\)f\$ and give it}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02666}02666 a default value of 1.0. Hence, if a Hookean constitutive}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02667}02667 law is instantiated with just one argument (the Poisson ratio \(\backslash\)f\$}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02668}02668 \(\backslash\)nu \(\backslash\)f\$), the stress is assumed to have been scaled on Young's}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02669}02669 modulus. If two arguments are provided, the second argument}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02670}02670 should be interpreted as the ratio of}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02671}02671 the material's Young's modulus to the reference stress }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02672}02672 \(\backslash\)f\$ \{\(\backslash\)cal S\} \(\backslash\)f\$ used in the non-\/dimensionalisation of the equations.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02673}02673 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02674}02674 \(\backslash\)subsubsection 2D\_solid 2D problems: Plane strain.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02675}02675 Many solid mechanics problems can be regarded as two-\/dimensional}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02676}02676 in the sense that the quantities of interest only depend on two}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02677}02677 spatial coordinates. In such problems it is important to consider what}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02678}02678 constraints the system is subjected to in the third direction -\/-\/ clearly}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02679}02679 all real solid bodies are three-\/dimensional!}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02680}02680 In plane strain problems, the displacements of material points are assumed}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02681}02681 to be parallel to the 2D plane spanned by the coordinates \(\backslash\)f\$x\_1}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02682}02682 \(\backslash\)f\$ and \(\backslash\)f\$ x\_2\(\backslash\)f\$, so that any displacements }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02683}02683 normal to this plane are suppressed. In this case, significant }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02684}02684 transverse stresses can develop.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02685}02685 Conversely, in plane stress problems, it is assumed that no stresses}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02686}02686 develop in the transverse direction; in this case we need}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02687}02687 to allow material particles to be displaced transversely.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02688}02688 Since we have formulated our problem in terms of positions }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02689}02689 (i.e. in terms of the displacement of material points), our formulation}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02690}02690 naturally produces a <B>plane strain</B> problem if we reduce}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02691}02691 the equations to two dimensions:}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02692}02692 We assume that the transverse displacement vanishes, }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02693}02693 while the remaining (in-\/plane) displacements are only }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02694}02694 functions of the in-\/plane coordinates, \(\backslash\)f\$ x\_1\(\backslash\)f\$ and \(\backslash\)f\$ x\_2\(\backslash\)f\$.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02695}02695 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02696}02696 It is important to remember that the 2D version of all equations needs to }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02697}02697 produce plane-\/strain behaviour when new, strain-\/energy-\/based }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02698}02698 constitutive equation classes are formulated:}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02699}02699 When implementing such strain-\/energy functions, recall that any}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02700}02700 invariants of metric tensors etc. are the invariants of the full}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02701}02701 3D quantities which are not necessarily the same as those}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02702}02702 of the corresponding 2D quantities.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02703}02703 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02704}02704 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02705}02705 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02706}02706 \(\backslash\)subsubsection isotropic\_growth Isotropic growth.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02707}02707 Many biological tissues undergo growth processes. For instance, the cells }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02708}02708 that make up a solid tumour divide regularly and as a result the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02709}02709 total mass of the tumour increases. If the growth }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02710}02710 occurs non-\/uniformly so that certain parts of the tumour grow faster}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02711}02711 than others, regions that grow more slowly restrain the expansion}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02712}02712 of their neighbours. This process can induce significant growth stresses.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02713}02713 The scenario is similar (but not identical) to that of thermal }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02714}02714 growth in which a non-\/uniform temperature distribution in }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02715}02715 a body creates thermal stresses. (The important difference between}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02716}02716 these two cases is that in the latter process mass is conserved -\/-\/}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02717}02717 thermal expansion only leads to an increase in the volume occupied}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02718}02718 by the material, whereas biological growth via cell division }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02719}02719 increases the mass of the tumour). }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02720}02720 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02721}02721 It is easy to incorporate such growth processes into our }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02722}02722 theoretical framework. The general idea is sketched in the }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02723}02723 following figure:}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02724}02724 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02725}02725 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02726}02726 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02727}02727 }

\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02746}02746 \(\backslash\)n <B> (Hypothetical) state U1:</B> The individual infinitesimal }

\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02749}02749 a stress-\/free state. The isotropic growth}

\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02776}02776 grown by different amounts they can (in general) not be (re-\/)assembled}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02777}02777 to form a continuous body without undergoing some deformation.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02778}02778 The deformation of the material elements (relative to their}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02779}02779 stress-\/free shape in the hypothetical, stress-\/free state N1) }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02780}02780 induces internal stresses -\/-\/ the so-\/called growth-\/stresses.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02781}02781 </TD>}

\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02791}02791 deformation (relative to their stress-\/free shape in state}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02792}02792 U1 (or, equivalently, U2), generates internal stresses which}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02793}02793 -\/ balance the applied loads,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02794}02794 -\/ keep all infinitesimal material elements in local equilibrium.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02795}02795 </TD>}

\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02804}02804 -\/ keep the material elements in local equilibrium.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02805}02805 </TD>}

\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02808}02808 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02809}02809 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02810}02810 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02811}02811 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02812}02812 We start our analysis with the stress-\/free (and }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02813}02813 "{}ungrown"{}) reference configuration "{}0"{} at the top of the diagram,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02814}02814 and initially follow the deformation shown in the left half}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02815}02815 of the sketch. In a first step, each infinitesimal material}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02816}02816 element in  the body is subjected to the same isotropic growth}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02817}02817 which changes its mass from  \(\backslash\)f\$\(\backslash\)mbox\{d\}M\(\backslash\)f\$ to}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02818}02818 \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)Gamma \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)mbox\{d\}M \(\backslash\)f\$. Assuming that the growth process does not}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02819}02819 change the density of the material, \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)Gamma\(\backslash\)f\$ also specifies}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02820}02820 the volumetric growth of the material. All material}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02821}02821 elements grow by the same amount, therefore the individual elements}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02822}02822 can be (re-\/)assembled to form a continuous body (state}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02823}02823 U2). In this state, the body is }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02824}02824 stress-\/free and, compared to the reference configuration "{}0"{},}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02825}02825 all lengths have increased by a factor of \(\backslash\)f\$\(\backslash\)Gamma\string^\{1/d\}\(\backslash\)f\$ }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02826}02826 where \(\backslash\)f\$ d \(\backslash\)f\$ is the body's spatial dimension (i.e. \(\backslash\)f\$d=2\(\backslash\)f\$ in }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02827}02827 the sketch above). The covariant basis vectors in this }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02828}02828 uniformly-\/grown, stress-\/free configuration are therefore given by}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02829}02829 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02830}02830 \(\backslash\)widetilde\{\(\backslash\)bf g\}\_i = \(\backslash\)Gamma\string^\{1/d\} \(\backslash\) \{\(\backslash\)bf g\}\_i,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02831}02831 \(\backslash\)f] }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02832}02832 the metric tensor is given by}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02833}02833 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02834}02834 \(\backslash\)widetilde\{g\_\{ij\}\} = \(\backslash\)Gamma\string^\{2/d\} \(\backslash\) g\_\{ij\},}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02835}02835 \(\backslash\)f] }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02836}02836 and the volume of an infinitesimal material element}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02837}02837 has increased from }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02838}02838 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02839}02839 dv = \(\backslash\)sqrt\{g\}  \(\backslash\) d\(\backslash\)xi\string^1 ... \(\backslash\) d\(\backslash\)xi\string^D}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02840}02840 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02841}02841 to }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02842}02842 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02843}02843 \(\backslash\)widetilde\{dv\} = \(\backslash\)Gamma \(\backslash\)sqrt\{g\} \(\backslash\) d\(\backslash\)xi\string^1 ... \(\backslash\) d\(\backslash\)xi\string^D }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02844}02844 \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) (29)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02845}02845 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02846}02846 We now subject the stress-\/free, uniformly-\/grown body to}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02847}02847 external loads and determine its deformation, using the principle}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02848}02848 of virtual displacements. Since the uniformly grown state "{}U2"{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02849}02849 is stress-\/free, we may regard it as the reference state for}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02850}02850 the subsequent deformation. The strain tensor that describes}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02851}02851 the deformation from the stress-\/free (and uniformly-\/grown) state "{}U2"{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02852}02852 to the final equilibrium configuration "{}UE"{} must therefore}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02853}02853 be defined as}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02854}02854 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02855}02855 \(\backslash\)gamma\_\{ij\} = \(\backslash\)frac\{1\}\{2\} \(\backslash\)left(G\_\{ij\} -\/ \(\backslash\)widetilde\{g\_\{ij\}\}\(\backslash\)right)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02856}02856  = \(\backslash\)frac\{1\}\{2\} \(\backslash\)left(G\_\{ij\} -\/ \(\backslash\)Gamma\string^\{2/D\} \(\backslash\) g\_\{ij\} \(\backslash\)right)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02857}02857 \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) (30)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02858}02858 \(\backslash\)f]}

\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02873}02873   \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) (31)}

\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02877}02877 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02878}02878 We will now consider the case of spatially non-\/uniform growth,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02879}02879 illustrated in the right half of the sketch. If the isotropic}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02880}02880 growth is spatially non-\/uniform, \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)Gamma = \(\backslash\)Gamma(\(\backslash\)xi\string^i)\(\backslash\)f\$,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02881}02881 the growth will try to expand all infinitesimal material }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02882}02882 elements isotropically -\/-\/ but each one by a different amount as}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02883}02883 illustrated by the hypothetical state N1 in which each material}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02884}02884 element has expanded to its stress-\/free state in which its}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02885}02885 metric tensor is given by}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02886}02886 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02887}02887 \(\backslash\)widetilde\{g\_\{ij\}\} = \(\backslash\)Gamma(\(\backslash\)xi\string^k) \(\backslash\) g\_\{ij\}.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02888}02888 \(\backslash\)f] }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02889}02889 Material elements will only be stress-\/free if the strain }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02890}02890 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02891}02891 \(\backslash\)gamma\_\{ij\} = \(\backslash\)frac\{1\}\{2\} \(\backslash\)left(G\_\{ij\} -\/ \(\backslash\)widetilde\{g\_\{ij\}\}\(\backslash\)right)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02892}02892  = \(\backslash\)frac\{1\}\{2\} \(\backslash\)left(G\_\{ij\} -\/ \(\backslash\)Gamma\string^\{2/D\}(\(\backslash\)xi\string^k) \(\backslash\) g\_\{ij\} \(\backslash\)right)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02893}02893 \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) (32)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02894}02894 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02895}02895 relative to their isotropically grown shape in state N1 is zero.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02896}02896 In general, the displacements induced by such an isotropic}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02897}02897 expansion will be}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02898}02898 incompatible and it would be impossible to (re-\/)assemble the }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02899}02899 individually grown material elements to a continuous body}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02900}02900 unless the material elements undergo some deformation. }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02901}02901 The elements' deformation relative to their}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02902}02902 stress-\/free shape in N1 will generate internal "{}growth-\/stresses"{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02903}02903 (stage N2). When subjected to external loads and body forces}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02904}02904 the body will undergo further deformations until the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02905}02905 the stress (generated by the particles' total deformation relative to}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02906}02906 their stress-\/free state N1) balances the applied loads.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02907}02907 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02908}02908 It is important to realise that, as in the case of spatially}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02909}02909 uniform growth, the strain defined by (30) is }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02910}02910 an intrinsic quantity that provides a measure of each particles' }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02911}02911 \(\backslash\)e local deformation relative to its stress-\/free shape in N1. }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02912}02912 The intermediate (and in the current case hypothetical), isotropically }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02913}02913 grown state N1 does not appear in the analysis -\/-\/ it only serves}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02914}02914 to define the stress-\/free shape for each infinitesimal}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02915}02915 material element. Equation (31) therefore}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02916}02916 remains valid.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02917}02917 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02918}02918 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02919}02919 \(\backslash\)subsubsection CartesianLagrangian Specialisation to a cartesian basis and finite element discretisation}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02920}02920 If the problem does not have any}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02921}02921 symmetries (e.g. axisymmetry) whose exploitation would reduce}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02922}02922 the spatial dimension of the problem, the most compact form}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02923}02923 of the equations is obtained by resolving all vectors into}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02924}02924 a fixed cartesian basis so that the undeformed position vector}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02925}02925 is given by}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02926}02926 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02927}02927 \{\(\backslash\)bf r\}(\(\backslash\)xi\string^j) = r\_i(\(\backslash\)xi\string^j) \(\backslash\) \{\(\backslash\)bf e\}\_i,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02928}02928  \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) (33)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02929}02929 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02930}02930 Similarly, we write }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02931}02931 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02932}02932 \{\(\backslash\)bf f\} = f\_i \(\backslash\) \{\(\backslash\)bf e\}\_i,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02933}02933 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02934}02934 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02935}02935 \{\(\backslash\)bf t\} = t\_i \(\backslash\) \{\(\backslash\)bf e\}\_i,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02936}02936 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02937}02937 and }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02938}02938 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02939}02939 \{\(\backslash\)bf R\}\string^\{(BC)\} = R\string^\{(BC)\}\_i \(\backslash\) \{\(\backslash\)bf e\}\_i.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02940}02940 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02941}02941 }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02942}02942 We use the Eulerian coordinates in the undeformed }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02943}02943 configuration as the Lagrangian coordinates so that}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02944}02944 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02945}02945 r\_i(\(\backslash\)xi\string^j) = \(\backslash\)xi\string^i. \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) (34)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02946}02946 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02947}02947 With this choice, the tangent vectors to the undeformed coordinate lines}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02948}02948 are the cartesian basis vectors}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02949}02949 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02950}02950 \{\(\backslash\)bf g\}\_i =  \{\(\backslash\)bf e\}\_i, }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02951}02951 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02952}02952 and the undeformed metric tensor is the Kronecker delta}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02953}02953 (the unit matrix)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02954}02954 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02955}02955 g\_\{ij\} = \(\backslash\)delta\_\{ij\}.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02956}02956 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02957}02957 We now expand the (unknown) deformed position vector in the same basis,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02958}02958 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02959}02959 \{\(\backslash\)bf R\}(\(\backslash\)xi\string^j) = R\_i(\(\backslash\)xi\string^j) \(\backslash\) \{\(\backslash\)bf e\}\_i,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02960}02960 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02961}02961 and derive a finite element approximation for this vector field}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02962}02962 from the principle of virtual displacements. For this purpose we decompose}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02963}02963 the undeformed body into a number of finite elements, using the}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02964}02964 standard mesh generation process described previously.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02965}02965 This establishes the Eulerian position \(\backslash\)f\$ X\_\{ij\}\string^\{(0)\} \(\backslash\)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02966}02966 (j=1,...,N) \(\backslash\)f\$ of the \(\backslash\)f\$ N \(\backslash\)f\$}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02967}02967 nodes in the body's undeformed configuration.}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02968}02968 Since the Eulerian coordinates of material points in the undeformed }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02969}02969 configuration coincide with their Lagrangian coordinates (see }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02970}02970 (34)), a finite-\/element representation of the }
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02971}02971 Lagrangian coordinates is established by writing}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02972}02972 \(\backslash\)f[}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02973}02973 \(\backslash\)xi\string^i = \(\backslash\)sum\_\{j=1\}\string^\{N\} \(\backslash\)Xi\_\{ij\} \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)psi\_j,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02974}02974 \(\backslash\)f]}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02975}02975 where \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)Xi\_\{ij\} = X\_\{ij\}\string^\{(0)\} \(\backslash\)f\$ is the \(\backslash\)f\$i\(\backslash\)f\$-\/th }

\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02978}02978 \(\backslash\)f\$\(\backslash\)psi\_j\(\backslash\)f\$ are, of course, represented by local shape functions, }

\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02983}02983 \(\backslash\)f]}

\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{leftovers_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02988}02988 \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\) \(\backslash\)   (35)}
